B, Material Processed

In October, the Station was provided by the’LIENVOY LP with 138
pages of dally resumes, from all lines, 15 pages of resumes from the Cuban
lines, 17 pages from the Czech lines and 121 pages from the Soviet lines,

In addition the taped reels from the Sovict and Czech lines were turned over
for the transcrtpton-of the Russian and Czech conversations,’ There were
also provided 44 picces of other miscellaneous matertal,

- C, Liaison

Because of the urgency of business during the month of Octeber, thy
COS met with LIERGO and LIELEGANT more frequently, LITENSOR exe
pressed his-grateluliess through LIELEGANT on providing him with reports®
‘on the political scene in the Far East count ries that he had visited, Qn 25
October, LITENSOR was given the report on the Cuban siiuation which was,
gent to the Station in DIR 44302, LITENSOR was also shown photos af the
Sovict missile bases in Cuba, After meeting with high-level Mexican efticials,
the Chief of Station reported in MEXL 2397 on thetr attitudes of the ULS..
quarantine of Cuba and the stopping of further progress on Soviet missile

bases there, ‘

D. Exploitation of Matertal

‘An example of information obtained through LIENVOY w:
attempt of Vicente Lombardo Toledano, prominent leftist Mexican po!
to make an Vappolnenvent witli the Mexican Government In regard to
Lombardo ‘Toledano was prompted by General Lazaro Cardenas to tryto
influence the President, (see MEX 2462)

E, Security

There were no known security problems,

F, Technical

Arnold F, Arehart, LIENVOY LP techniclan, made a trip to Head>
quarters on 19 October to plan with Headquarter’s personel the setting up of
tne new LIENVOY LP,

G, Production

During October, LIENVOY produced the thirty-four (34) reports
listed in the attachment, ‘The usual large amount of CE personality and
operational material was obtained in adJition to the (auached) dissemiaable

reports,

B, Materlal Processed

In August, the LIENVOY LP provided the Statton with 133 pages of
_ dally resumes, 40 pages of resumes from the Cuban lines and 35 other
pieces of matertal. There were also provided 115 pages of resumes from
the Soviet tines and 63 pages from the Czech lines,

CC. Exploitation of Material : :
The following-are exaniples of information obtaincd through LIENVOY.

1, Ina telephone conversation from San Luis Potosi, Col.
Renato Vega Amador, DFS Chief, told Capt, de la Barrera of the
Mexico City DFS: that- “things are happening in San.Luis Potosi",
and that “something'bad would happen” in Monterrey and Mexico
City against the Federal Government and that of the State of San
Luis Potost, (MEXI 1600)

2,. Joe Nordmann, Sccretary of the International Assocation of
Democratic Lawyers (IADL}, spoke with Angelica Arcnal de Alfaro
Siquciro# about his plan to see the President of Mexico to have David
Alfaro Siquetros released from prison. (MEXI 1676)

3. . According to employees of the Prensa Latina, employces had

not been paid for some time and the financial situation of the Agency
was “desperate”, (MEXI 167d)

D, Liaison : a : i ate

On 3 August, Chief of Station met with LITENSOR to give him a re-
port on Cuauhtemoc Cardenas, Through LIELEGANT on 8 August, Chief
of Station was told that Cardenas would not be a candidate for “Water
Commissloner’ in the Mexicali area, (MEXT 1652)

in MEXI £773, it was requested of Headquarters that briefing papers
vn Indonesia, Japan ‘and India be made available for LITENSOR's use on
his approaching visit to these countries in late September, These were
pouched io Mexico City Chief of Station accordiag to DIR 31814,

E. Security

No security problems were encountered during the menth,

F, Technical

The LP dase house continues to operate without any difficulties, The
1 covering of the base.house Moor with linoleum sometime ago has tremen-

dously helped in keeping the dust down and co keep the machines In excellent
working condition,

indead, doing a good Job of reviewing the LIZNVOY take, following up leads
and forwarding positive information to-Haadquartecs,

that the Staticn is avare of the operational leads presented through LIENVOY
but {t fe roalfzed that the Mexico City Station probably does not have the
aeseta to prouptly follow up all the leads presented, While Headquacters
does not wish to place a burden on the Station by requesting detailed reporting
on tho action teken on LISWVOY leads, Headquarters feels that the Station wight
inform Headquarters with sone regularity wiat ts being donc, It is suggested
that the Station include in ite Monthly Activities Zeport under Section A.
“Exploitation of Material Obtained", general statecents concerntag any out-
standing exploitation of leads, sueh as ia done in the LIFPAT Monthly

Reports ( HNQAS15595, 31 August 1260),

MEMORANDUM FOR: Chief, wH/3

SUBJECt: CW Signals on Telephone Tap

REFERENCE:

10 August 1960

HMMA-14977, 18 May 1960

Atechnical analysis of referonceltap indicates that the
CW Morse signals probably were picked up incidental to the primary
tap and did not actually occur on Line #2, This is borne out both
from a technical standpoint (signal to noise ratio, oxtraneous CW
als, ete.) as well as from the context of the messages them-
os, The latter, ao will be noted in the attached transcript,

primarily concern arrivals and departures of what appear to be
small maritime vousels, The two radio ‘calls mentioned, t,o.
“XBRB2" and "XBRP", are listed in the International Call Sign

Book as follows:

XBRB - Vera Cruz 19-10N, 96-15W)

XBRP - Pichilingue (24-12N, 110-20 W)

The originating station in this case was Pichilingue,

2, Matt ete ore 13 some good reason why a port
enn on the west coast of Mexico would be sending traflic of
this nature to an cast coast port, However, jst how these _
particular signals happened to be picked up ontim Brooks line
is open to conjecture, It is our guess that it probably was due

to one of the following reasons:

a, Aradiotranamitter may be situated near the
tap and is serving as a relay station between Pichilingue
and Vera Gruz, If this is the case it may be yiving off
strong radio frequency signals which possibly are being
rectified by the tap itself,



caer aeaee nie Stbas: a :
ele

ieee b, The equipment used in conjunction with the tap
: may be servitig as a poor radio receivar, using the telephone
: line as an antenna, a
€. The CW signals possibly are being picked up
inductively,-i,e, from another phone line which is in
: close proximity to Line #2, This theory seems-unlikely,
H however, since the transmission of CW signals from one
coast to the other via telephone lines would be a slow and .
impractical procedure, st
. he afyaarWoer
3, From’the standpoint of technical interest, we would
appreciate being advised if and when the Stztiow,iz able to sub=
stantiate any of the above conjectures. Gare. BS to
furnish additional analysis and transcripts should similar signals
be noted in the future,
hee:
oe A

WILLIAM K, HARVEY
Chici, FI/ Division D
